#  CPUC Annual Reports
As part of its mission to serve the public, and as required by state law, the CPUC provides the Governor and Legislature an Annual Report on its activities for the prior year and a look ahead at the work expected over the next 12 months. 
## Summary of Annual Reports to the Legislature
Each year the CPUC issues an Annual Report to the Legislature highlighting activities and providing a work plan for the coming year. See our Annual Reports below.
For Gas Safety and Reliability Branch (GSRB) and Electric Safety and Reliability Branch (ESRB) incidents reports, please visit this [page](https://www.cpuc.ca.gov/regulatory-services/safety/annual-electric-and-gas-incidents). 
For other reports to the Legislature (on energy, telco, etc.) see [Reports to the Legislature](https://www.cpuc.ca.gov/about-cpuc/divisions/office-of-governmental-affairs) on our Governmental Affairs page.

## REPORT TO THE LEGISLATURE
Resolution of Proceedings, Disposition of Applications for Rehearing, and
* * *
Commissioner Presence at Hearings

**Alice Reynolds**
**President**
**John Reynolds**
**Karen Douglas**
**Matthew Baker**
**Commissioners**
Darcie L. Houck
* * *
Submitted: February 20, 2026
* * *
## STATE OF CALIFORNIA GAVIN NEWSOM, Governor
PUBLIC UTILITIES COMMISSION
* * *
## _505 VAN NESS AVENUE_
SAN FRANCISCO, CA 94102-3298
* * *
PUBLIC UTILITIES COMMISSION REPORT PURSUANT TO PUBLIC UTILITIES CODE SECTION 910.1
* * *
Introduction
* * *
As the state’s primary regulator of investor-owned electric, gas, water, transportation, and telecommunication services, the California Public Utilities Commission (CPUC) is responsible for the development of effective regulatory constructs to ensure that these services are delivered safely, affordably, reliably, and environmentally responsibly. The CPUC carries out this important task through the management of public decision-making processes, known as proceedings, that solicit the expertise, perspectives, and input from stakeholder groups representing a wide range of interests and views. These proceedings ultimately lead to the creation, modification, or improvement of new and existing rules that are designed to achieve public interest objectives for the utility services overseen by the CPUC.
* * *
Public Utilities Code Section 910.1 requires the CPUC to report annually on the status of its proceedings, specifically, on timeliness in resolving cases, information on the disposition of applications for rehearing, and the number of days that Commissioners presided in hearings. The CPUC submits this report for the reporting period of calendar year 2025.
* * *
In addition, Public Utilities Code Section 1701.1 et seq. requires that regulatory matters before the CPUC be resolved within certain time periods, depending on the categorization of a proceeding. Prior to January 1, 2017, Public Utilities Code Sections 1701.1 et seq., the requirement for scoping memos and the statutory deadlines, did not apply to proceedings that were not subject to evidentiary hearing. However, Senate Bill 215 (Leno, Stats. 2016, ch. 807), amended Sections 1701.1 et seq. to extend their provisions to all proceedings regardless of whether they are subject to evidentiary hearing. Additional reporting requirements related to Commissioner attendance at hearings and workshops were added by Assembly Bill 1532 (Stats. 2025, Ch. 205).
* * *
There are four types of proceeding categories: adjudicatory, ratesetting, quasi-legislative, and catastrophic wildfire. Adjudicatory proceedings investigate and adjudicate possible violations of state or CPUC rules and must be resolved within 12 months. Ratesetting proceedings set or investigate rates that regulated entities charge customers; quasi-legislative
* * *
**Page 2**
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1
* * *
596761399 proceedings establish policies or rules affecting regulated entities. Both ratesetting and quasi-legislative proceedings must be resolved within 18 months, unless a longer deadline is set by the assigned Commissioner’s scoping memo or a CPUC order extending the statutory time period. Finally, in catastrophic wildfire proceedings, a proposed decision must be issued within 12 months.
* * *
CPUC proceedings are comprehensive, stakeholder informed decision-making processes that focus on producing the most desirable regulatory solutions to some of the state’s most critical electric, gas, telecommunications, water, and transportation utility issues. The CPUC also hears individual customer complaints against a utility. A proceeding is closed when key matters have been decided or are considered fully resolved by the parties. At times, proceedings that have had all substantive issues decided may remain open or be reopened because of stakeholder objections. These objections may take the form of applications for rehearing, petitions for modification, and various motions. CPUC proceedings can be complex and require the consideration of all perspectives provided by stakeholders throughout the proceeding. Before reaching a decision on regulatory and policy matters, Administrative Law Judges and Commissioners carefully review and consider the contributions of stakeholders, including formal testimony, comments, and reply comments to the Rulings and Proposed Decisions in a proceeding, keeping in mind the importance of resolving issues in a timely manner. Stakeholders to proceedings, who typically become parties to the proceeding, include the regulated investor-owned utilities, industry trade associations, consumer advocacy groups, non-profit organizations, local governments, and other interested participants. Participation in proceedings by these organizations is critical to ensure that the decisions made are well-informed and provide balanced solutions to the complex regulatory issues before the CPUC.
* * *
As described in this report, 171 out of 173 proceedings resolved by the CPUC in 2025 that were subject to statutory deadlines were completed consistent with statutory timeframes, either due to resolution within the statutory deadlines, or because a scoping memo establishing a longer deadline, or a timely extension order, was issued as permitted by law. This report provides details regarding whether proceedings were resolved in a timely manner with or without extension orders. More detailed information is contained in the attached Appendices A-K. Appendix L reports the days that Commissioners attended hearings, Appendix M reports on Commissioner attendance at proceeding-related workshops, and Appendix N reports information on the disposition of applications for rehearing.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 3
* * *
596761399 Lastly, in an effort to improve its decision-making processes, the CPUC continuously assesses and reassesses its management of proceedings. Improvements are focused on ensuring that these proceedings are accessible to interested stakeholders, preserve their due process rights as parties and ultimately lead to a resolution of matters in a reasonable timeframe. As the CPUC continues to develop refinements to decision-making processes that balance timeliness with thoughtful public participation and effective record development, the CPUC is always open to hearing the innovative ideas of the public, stakeholders, and the Legislature.
* * *
Description of Attached Appendices A-M
* * *
## _Appendix A – Proceedings Initiated Before January 1, 2017, not Subject to Evidentiary Hearings, Active_
During 2025 (Resolved and not Resolved)
* * *
## _Appendix A lists proceedings active during 2025 that were initiated prior to January 1, 2017, and not subject to_
evidentiary hearings. Of the 1 proceeding, 1 was resolved during 2025.
* * *
## _Appendix B – Complaints Under the Expedited Complaint Procedure, Active During 2025_
## _Appendix B lists 60 Expedited Complaint Proceedings (ECP) that are small complaint cases handled under_
special procedures analogous to “small claims” court. These proceedings are not subject to statutory deadlines. We are
* * *
reporting these matters separately because the CPUC has adopted more aggressive timelines for these cases than the statutory timelines for other proceedings. The CPUC has established an informal 132-day target for this type of proceeding to be resolved.
* * *
During 2025, 36 of these 60 proceedings were resolved. 24 proceedings remain active.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 4
* * *
596761399
* * *
## _Appendix C – Proceedings Active During 2025 – Proceedings Resolved_
During 2025, the CPUC timely resolved 171 proceedings (25 adjudicatory, 140 ratesetting, and 7 quasi
* * *
legislative). 2 proceedings did not meet the prescribed statutory deadline.
* * *
## _Appendix D – Proceedings Active During 2025 – Proceedings not Resolved_
During 2025, there was 1 active, unresolved proceeding that was initiated prior to January 1, 2017, and subject to
* * *
an evidentiary hearing, and 271 active, unresolved proceedings that were initiated after January 1, 2017. 270 proceedings (45 adjudicatory, 36 quasi-legislative, 171 ratesetting, 2 Catastrophic Wildfire, and 1 Adjudicatory/Ratesetting) are currently on schedule, taking into account statutory deadlines, orders extending statutory timeframes, and scoping memos establishing deadlines that in some instances exceed basic statutory timeframes. One proceeding was active but had not been timely extended as of December 31, 2025. One proceeding is addressing rehearing-related issues and categorization will be addressed as necessary if the CPUC subsequently grants rehearing.
* * *
## _Appendix E – Petitions for Valuation of Utility Property_
Petitions for Valuation of Utility Property are statutorily mandated proceedings subject to the requirements set
* * *
forth in Public Utilities Code Sections 1401-1421. Appendix E shows that one such proceeding was active during 2025.
* * *
## _Appendix F – Petitions for Rulemaking_
Petitions for Rulemaking are statutorily mandated proceedings subject to the deadlines in Public Utilities Code
* * *
Section 1708.5. The CPUC is mandated to issue a decision in this type of proceeding within six months. Appendix F shows that 1 such proceeding was resolved in 2025, and 1 remains active.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 5
* * *
596761399
* * *
## _Appendix G – Citation Appeals and General Order 156 Appeals_
Resolution ALJ-377 established the Citation Appeal and General Order 156 Appeal process (April 28, 2020)
* * *
based on the pilot program established by ALJ-299 (June 26, 2014). Under ALJ-377, appellate records are easily accessible, thus enhancing due process in these expeditious proceedings. Appendix G shows that 31 such appeals were active during 2025 and that the CPUC has issued 17 resolutions. 14 appeals are active.
* * *
## _Appendix HRequests for Hearing on Administrative Enforcement Orders Active During Calendar_
Year 2025
* * *
Resolution M-4846 established the process to Request a Hearing on an Administrative Enforcement Order. Under Resolution M-4846, requests for hearing follow the procedural rules set forth in Resolution ALJ-377 that provide easily accessible appellate records thereby enhancing due process and transparency of the CPUC Enforcement Policy. 2 proceedings were active during 2025. 1 proceeding was resolved during 2025.
* * *
## _Appendix I – 60-90 Day Period for Adoption of Decision_
The Legislature has also established guidelines for the length of time between the issuance of a proposed
* * *
decision and the adoption of a final decision by the CPUC, applicable to all ratesetting proceedings and to quasi legislative proceedings requiring a hearing. The guidelines are either 60 or 90 days depending on certain circumstances.
* * *
During 2025, the CPUC considered 114 proposed decisions subject to these guidelines. 14 proposed decisions are pending resolution. The CPUC adopted 100 decisions subject to these guidelines. 90 decisions were adopted within the guidelines. 10 proposed decisions were resolved outside the guidelines.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 6 596761399
* * *
## _Appendix J – Issuance of Presiding Officer Decisions and Proposed Decisions_
The Legislature has also established guidelines for the length of time between the submission of a matter for
* * *
decision and the issuance of the proposed decision. During 2025, the CPUC issued 11 presiding officer decisions and 102 proposed decisions in such proceedings. Out of these 113 decisions, 44 were issued within the 60-day and 90-day timelines. One proceeding required oral arguments after the proposed decisions was issued; consequently the submission time was inapplicable.
* * *
## _Appendix K – Issuance of Extension Orders and Scoping Memos_
The Legislature has also established a process for extending the statutory deadlines through issuance of an
* * *
extension order. During 2025, the CPUC issued 121 extension orders in 113 separate proceedings (more than one extension order was issued in some proceedings), including proceedings which remained open at the end of 2025. The assigned Commissioners issued 173 scoping memos (including amended scoping memos) in 170 proceedings.
* * *
## _Appendix L – Commissioner Attendance_
Public Utilities Code Section 910.1 requires the commission to annually submit a report to the Legislature on the
* * *
days that commissioners presided over and attended hearings. AB 1532, effective October 1, 2025, revised these statutory requirements. Prior to its enactment, Commission attendance information was not maintained in the format specified. The figures presented reflect the requested information in the format now required under Public Utilities Code Section 910.1. For reporting on commissioner attendance at hearings, the report shall include reporting based on attendance at all types of hearings, including by all of the following: (1) H earing type, including, but not limited to, prehearing conferences, evidentiary hearings, public participation hearings, and workshops. (2) P roceeding type, including quasi-legislative, an adjudication, a rate-setting, or a catastrophic wildfire proceeding. (3) Ind ustry type, including electric, gas, water, telecommunications, or transportation.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 7
* * *
596761399
* * *
## _Appendix M – Information on Disposition of Applications for Rehearing_
## _Appendix M reports information on the disposition of applications for rehearing in 2025._
Conclusion
* * *
In summary, this report, submitted in compliance with Public Utilities Code Section 910.1, provides the public and the Legislature information on CPUC action in formal proceedings. Specifically, 542 proceedings were active at the CPUC during the 2025 reporting period. During 2025, 229 of these proceedings were resolved. 98.8% of the proceedings subject to statutory deadlines were resolved consistent with statutory requirements, taking into account scoping memos, which in some instances set deadlines longer than basic statutory timeframes, and orders extending the statutory timeframes adopted by the CPUC, as permitted by statute. The CPUC is committed to achieving compliance with the statutory guidelines.

* * *
* Commission Resolution M-4846 established the process to Request a Hearing on an Administrative Enforcement Order. Under Resolution M 4846, requests for hearing will follow the procedural rules set forth in Resolution ALJ-377 that provide easily accessible appellate records thereby enhancing due process and transparency of the Commission Enforcement Policy. ** These type of proceedings are not assigned to Commissioners. Closed Session Meeting 20* 20 20 20 20 Commission Voting Meeting 18* 17 18 18 18 Evidentiary Hearing 11 0 0 0 Legislative Oversight Hearing 50 0 0 1 Oral Argument 33 3 3 1 Prehearing Conference 28 6 0 1 6 Public Participation Hearing 11 0 1 2 1 6 APPENDIX L Public Utilities Code Section 910.1 requires the commission to annually submit a report to the Legislature on the days that commissioners presided over and attended hearings. AB 1532, effective October 1, 2025, revised these statutory requirements. Prior to its enactment, Commission attendance info rmation was not maintained in the format specified. The figures presented reflect the requested information in t he format now required under Public Utilities Code Section 910.1. For reporting on commissioner attendance at hearings, the report shall include reporting based on attendance at all types of hearings, including by all of the following: (1) H earing type, including, but not limited to, preheari ng conferences, evidentiary hearings, public participation hearings, and w orkshops. (2) P roceeding type, including quasi-legislative, an adjudication, a rate-setting, or a catastrophic wildfire proceeding. (3) Industry type, including electric, gas, water, telecommunications, or transportation. Commissioner Karen Douglas Commissioner Matthew Baker COMMISSIONERS ATTENDANCE AT PROCEEDING-RELATED HEARINGS AND WORKSHOPS Hearing Type: prehearing conference, evidentiary hearings, public participation hearings, workshop, or other: Reporting on Commissioner Attendance at Hearings, Pursuant to Public Utilities Code Section 910.1 President Alice Reynolds Commissioner Darcie L. ## STATE OF CALIFORNIA EDMUND G. BROWN JR., Governor
PUBLIC UTILITIES COMMISSION
* * *
## _505 VAN NESS AVENUE_
SAN FRANCISCO, CA 94102-3298
* * *
PUBLIC UTILITIES COMMISSION REPORT PURSUANT TO PUBLIC UTILITIES CODE SECTION 910.1
* * *
Introduction
* * *
Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 requires that the California Public Utilities Commission (CPUC) report on the number of formal proceedings where resolution exceeded the time periods prescribed in scoping memos and the number of days that Commissioners presided in hearings. It further requires that the Commission submit the report to the Governor and Legislature no later than February 1 of each year. As described in this report for calendar year 2016, all proceedings resolved at the Commission during 2016 that were subject to statutory deadlines were completed consistent with statutory timeframes, either due to resolution within the statutory deadlines or because a scoping memo establishing a longer deadline or timely extension order was issued as permitted by law. This report provides details regarding whether proceedings were resolved in a timely manner with or without extension orders. More detailed information is contained in the attached Appendices A-K.
* * *
Pub. Util. Code Sections 1701.1 et al. apply to cases filed after 1998 that were subject to hearing at the Commission.
* * *
## _1 These statutes require that matters be resolved within certain time periods, depending on the_
categorization of a proceeding. Generally, adjudicatory matters must be resolved within 12 months and ratesetting and
* * *
quasi-legislative matters are to be resolved within 18 months of the issuance of the scoping memo ruling, unless a longer deadline is set by the CPUC through issuance of a scoping memo or order extending the statutory time period.
* * *
## _2 A_
proceeding has been resolved when the main issues have been decided such that the proceeding could usually be
* * *
closed. At times, proceedings that have had all substantive issues decided may remain open or are “re-opened” because of other issues, such as petitions for modifications, various motions, or requests for intervenor compensation.
* * *
## Effective January 1, 2017, these statutes apply regardless of whether they are subject to hearing.
## _2 Effective January 1, 2017, ratesetting and quasi-legislative matters are to be resolved within 18 months from initiation._
**Page 2**
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Public Utilities Code Section 910.1
* * *
172781982 In addition to data related to proceedings that were subject to hearings and statutory deadlines, this report contains important case management information on other proceedings as well, in the interest of providing transparency, public access, and statutory compliance.
* * *
Description of Attached Appendices A-K
* * *
## _Appendix A – Formal Proceedings not Subject to Hearings, Active During this Reporting_
**Period**
## _Appendix A lists the 280 cases active during the time period that were not subject to hearings. This year many of_
these proceedings are ratesetting or adjudicatory matters that were conducted without formal evidentiary hearings. Also,
* * *
this appendix lists 30 quasi-legislative matters that were processed through the exchange of written documents and formal evidentiary hearings were not required.
* * *
These proceedings are not subject to statutory deadline. Of the 280 cases, 189 were resolved in a time consistent with the deadlines set by the CPUC in scoping memos. The remaining 81 proceedings are currently active and on schedule.
* * *
## _Appendix B – Complaints Under the Expedited Complaint Procedure, Active During the_
**Reporting Period**
## _Appendix B lists 38 Expedited Complaint Proceedings (ECP) that are small complaint cases handled under special_
procedures analogous to “small claims” court. These proceedings are not subject to statutory deadlines. We are reporting
* * *
these matters separately because the Commission has adopted more aggressive timelines for these cases than the statutory timelines for other proceedings. The Commission has established an informal 132-day target for this type of proceeding to be resolved.
* * *
During the reporting period, 33 of these 38 cases were resolved. Five proceedings remain active.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Public Utilities Code Section 910.1 Page 3
* * *
172781982
* * *
## _Appendix C – Formal Proceedings Subject to Hearings, Active During the Reporting Period_
Proceedings Resolved on Schedule
* * *
During the reporting period, the Commission timely resolved 42 (37 ratesetting and 5 adjudicatory) proceedings subject to evidentiary hearings.
* * *
## _Appendix D – Formal Proceedings Subject to Hearing, Currently Active and on Schedule_
## _Appendix D contains cases subject to hearing that are not yet resolved and currently still active. There are 118_
such cases – 27 adjudicatory, 5 quasi-legislative, 1 quasi-legislative/adjudicatory, 4 quasi-legislative/ratesetting, and 81
* * *
ratesetting. All of these cases are currently on schedule taking into account statutory deadlines, orders extending statutory timeframes, and scoping memos establishing deadlines that in some instances exceed statutory timeframes.
* * *
## _Appendix E – Petitions for Rulemaking_
Petitions for Rulemaking are statutorily mandated proceedings subject to the deadlines in Pub. Util. Code Section
* * *
1708.5. The Commission is mandated to issue a decision in this type of proceeding within six months. Appendix E shows that four such proceedings were active during the reporting period and that the Commission has issued two timely decisions. Two petitions are active and currently on schedule.
* * *
## _Appendix F – Citation Appeals and General Order 156 Appeals_
The Commission, in Resolution ALJ-299, signed on June 26, 2014, established a Pilot Program Citation Appeal
* * *
and General Order 156 Appellate Rules, effective January 1, 2015. Under this pilot program, these appellate records will be easily accessible, thus enhancing due process in these expeditious proceedings. Appendix F shows that thirteen such appeals were active during the reporting period and that the Commission has issued nine resolutions addressing the appeals. Four appeals are active.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Public Utilities Code Section 910.1 Page 4
* * *
172781982
* * *
## _Appendix G – Citation Appeals and General Order 156 Appeals_
The Federal Telecommunications Act of 1996 created a new type of proceeding with aggressive timelines. These
* * *
proceedings are not subject to the SB 960 timelines. During the reporting period two of these proceedings were active at the Commission. The Commission has issued two decisions within the federally mandated 9-month timeline.
* * *
## _Appendix H – Commissioner Attendance_
## _Appendix H reports the Commissioner attendance at hearings during the period. The table shows that_
Commissioners attended 83 days of hearings and presided during 27 of those 83 days.
* * *
## _Appendix I – 60-90 Day Compliance_
The Legislature has also established guidelines for the length of time between the issuance of a proposed decision
* * *
and the adoption of a final decision by the Commission, applicable to ratesetting and quasi-legislative proceedings requiring a hearing. The guidelines are either 60 or 90 days depending on certain circumstances.
* * *
During the period, the Commission considered 36 proposed decisions in proceedings subject to these guidelines. The Commission adopted 35 final decisions in such proceedings. In 30 instances, the final decision was adopted within the guidelines and in five instances; the final decision was issued later than the period specified in the guidelines. One proposed decision was withdrawn.
* * *
## _Appendix J – Issuance of Presiding Officer Decisions and Proposed Decisions_
For proceedings that require a hearing, the Legislature has also established guidelines for the length of time
* * *
between the submission of a matter for decision and the issuance of the proposed decision. During the period, the Commission issued one presiding officer decisions and 31 proposed decisions in such proceedings. Out of these 32 decisions, 20 (62.5%) were issued within the mandatory 60-day and 90-day timelines. This percentage is higher than 2015 by 4.5% despite the Administrative Law Judges Division experiencing significant turnover during the past year. During 2016, the Administrative Law Judges Division hired four new full-time judges, who are in the process of being trained. At the same time, the Division lost five judges due to retirements and new job opportunities. Despite these challenging staffing issues, we are looking at ways to achieve better results in 2017.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Public Utilities Code Section 910.1 Page 5
* * *
172781982
* * *
## _Appendix K – Issuance of Extension Orders_
The Legislature has also established a process for extending the statutory deadlines through issuance of an
* * *
extension order. During 2016, the Commission issued 34 extension orders in 20 separate proceedings (more than one extension order was issued in some proceedings), including proceedings which remained open at the end of 2016. Of the 287 proceedings resolved in 2016, 42 proceedings were subject to statutory deadlines and there were 13 proceedings where extension orders were issued.
* * *
Conclusion
* * *
In summary, this report, submitted in compliance with Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1, provides the public and the legislature information on Commission action in formal proceedings. Specifically, 497 proceedings were active at the Commission during the 2016 reporting period. 287 of these proceedings were resolved during 2016. 42 of the proceedings that were resolved were subject to statutory deadlines. 100% of the proceedings subject to statutory deadlines were resolved consistent with statutory requirements taking into account scoping memos, which in some instances set deadlines longer than statutory timeframes, and orders extending the statutory timeframes adopted by the Commission, as permitted by statute. The Commission is committed to continuing to achieve full compliance with the mandatory statutory deadlines, transparent and accessible proceedings and procedures, and will work toward compliance with the statutory guidelines.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Public Utilities Code Section 910.1 Page 6
* * *
172781982

SAN FRANCISCO, CA 94102-3298
* * *
PUBLIC UTILITIES COMMISSION REPORT PURSUANT TO PUBLIC UTILITIES CODE SECTION 910.1
* * *
Introduction
* * *
As the state’s primary regulator of investor-owned electric, gas, water, transportation and telecommunication services, the California Public Utilities Commission (Commission) is responsible for the development of effective regulatory constructs to ensure that these services are delivered safely, affordably, reliably, and environmentally responsibly. The Commission carries out this important task through the management of public decision-making processes, known as proceedings, that solicit the expertise, perspectives, and input from stakeholder groups representing a wide range of interests and views. These proceedings ultimately lead to the creation, modification, or improvement of new and existing rules that are designed to achieve public interest objectives for the utility services overseen by the Commission.
* * *
Public Utilities Code Section 910.1 requires the Commission to report annually on the status of its proceedings, specifically, on timeliness in resolving cases, information on the disposition of applications for rehearing, and the number of days that Commissioners presided in hearings. The Commission submits this report for the reporting period of calendar year 2024.
* * *
In addition, Public Utilities Code Section 1701.1 et seq. requires that regulatory matters before the Commission be resolved within certain time periods, depending on the categorization of a proceeding. Prior to January 1, 2017, Public Utilities Code Sections 1701.1 et seq., the requirement for scoping memos and the statutory deadlines, did not apply to proceedings that were not subject to evidentiary hearing. However, Senate Bill 215 (Leno, Stats. 2016, ch. 807), amended Sections 1701.1 et seq. to extend their provisions to all proceedings regardless of whether they are subject to evidentiary hearing.
* * *
There are four types of proceeding categories: adjudicatory, ratesetting, quasi-legislative, and catastrophic wildfire. Adjudicatory proceedings investigate and adjudicate possible violations of state or Commission rules and must be resolved within 12 months. Ratesetting proceedings set or investigate rates that regulated entities charge customers; quasi-legislative
* * *
**Page 2**
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1
* * *
555639775 proceedings establish polices or rules affecting regulated entities. Both ratesetting and quasi-legislative proceedings must be resolved within 18 months, unless a longer deadline is set by the assigned Commissioner’s scoping memo or a Commission order extending the statutory time period. Finally, in catastrophic wildfire proceedings, a proposed decision must be issued within 12 months.
* * *
Commission proceedings are comprehensive, stakeholder informed decision-making processes that focus on producing the most desirable regulatory solutions to some of the state’s most critical electric, gas, telecommunications, water, and transportation utility issues. The Commission also hears individual customer complaints against a utility. A proceeding is closed when key matters have been decided or are considered fully resolved by the parties. At times, proceedings that have had all substantive issues decided may remain open or be reopened because of stakeholder objections. These objections may take the form of applications for rehearing, petitions for modification, and various motions. Commission proceedings can be complex and require the consideration of all perspectives provided by stakeholders throughout the proceeding. Before reaching a decision on regulatory and policy matters, Administrative Law Judges and Commissioners carefully review and consider the contributions of stakeholders, including formal testimony, comments, and reply comments to the Rulings and Proposed Decisions in a proceeding, keeping in mind the importance of resolving issues in a timely manner. Stakeholders to proceedings, who typically become parties to the proceeding, include the regulated investor-owned utilities, industry trade associations, consumer advocacy groups, non-profit organizations, local governments, and other interested participants. Participation in proceedings by these organizations is critical to ensure that the decisions made are well informed and provide balanced solutions to the complex regulatory issues before the Commission.
* * *
As described in this report, 170 out of 173 proceedings resolved by the Commission in 2024 that were subject to statutory deadlines were completed consistent with statutory timeframes, either due to resolution within the statutory deadlines, or because a scoping memo establishing a longer deadline, or a timely extension order, was issued as permitted by law. This report provides details regarding whether proceedings were resolved in a timely manner with or without extension orders. More detailed information is contained in the attached Appendices A-J. Appendix K reports the days that Commissioners presided in hearings, and Appendix L reports information on the disposition of applications for rehearing.
* * *
Lastly, in an effort to improve its decision-making processes, the Commission continuously assesses and reassesses its management of proceedings. Improvements are focused on ensuring that these proceedings are accessible to interested
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 3
* * *
555639775 stakeholders, preserve their due process rights as parties and ultimately lead to a resolution of matters in a reasonable timeframe. As the Commission continues to develop refinements to decision-making processes that balance timeliness with thoughtful public participation and effective record development, the Commission is always open to hearing the innovative ideas of the public, stakeholders, and the Legislature.
* * *
Description of Attached Appendices A-L
* * *
## _Appendix A – Proceedings Initiated Before January 1, 2017, not Subject to Evidentiary Hearings, Active_
During 2024 (Resolved and not Resolved)
* * *
## _Appendix A lists proceedings active during 2024 that were initiated prior to January 1, 2017, and not subject to_
evidentiary hearings. Of the 3 proceedings, 2 were resolved during 2024. The remaining proceeding is currently active and
* * *
on schedule.
* * *
## _Appendix B – Complaints Under the Expedited Complaint Procedure, Active During 2024_
## _Appendix B lists 53 Expedited Complaint Proceedings (ECP) that are small complaint cases handled under special_
procedures analogous to “small claims” court. These proceedings are not subject to statutory deadlines. We are reporting
* * *
these matters separately because the Commission has adopted more aggressive timelines for these cases than the statutory timelines for other proceedings. The Commission has established an informal 132-day target for this type of proceeding to be resolved.
* * *
During 2024, 33 of these 53 proceedings were resolved. Twenty proceedings remain active.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 4
* * *
555639775
* * *
## _Appendix C – Proceedings Active During 2024 – Proceedings Resolved_
During 2024, the Commission timely resolved 170 proceedings (25 adjudicatory, 141 ratesetting, 3 quasi-legislative;
* * *
and 1 proceeding resolved rehearing-related issues that were not categorized). 3 proceedings did not meet the prescribed statutory deadline.
* * *
## _Appendix D – Proceedings Active During 2024 – Proceedings not Resolved_
During 2024, there was 1 active, unresolved proceeding that was initiated prior to January 1, 2017, and subject to an
* * *
evidentiary hearing, and 259 active, unresolved proceedings that were initiated after January 1, 2017. 259 proceedings (31 adjudicatory, 35 quasi-legislative and 186 ratesetting) are currently on schedule, taking into account statutory deadlines, orders extending statutory timeframes, and scoping memos establishing deadlines that in some instances exceed basic statutory timeframes. Seven proceedings are pending assignment and have not ben categorized. One proceeding was active but had not been timely extended as of December 31, 2024. Three proceedings are addressing rehearing-related issues and categorization will be addressed as necessary if the Commission subsequently grants rehearing.
* * *
## _Appendix E – Petitions for Valuation of Utility Property_
Petitions for Valuation of Utility Property are statutorily mandated proceedings subject to the deadlines in Public
* * *
Utilities Code Sections 1401-1421. Appendix E shows that one such proceeding was active during 2024 and currently on schedule.
* * *
## _Appendix F – Petitions for Rulemaking_
Petitions for Rulemaking are statutorily mandated proceedings subject to the deadlines in Public Utilities Code Section
* * *
1708.5. The Commission is mandated to issue a decision in this type of proceeding within six months. Appendix F shows that three such proceedings were resolved in 2024, and one remains active.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 5
* * *
555639775
* * *
## _Appendix G – Citation Appeals and General Order 156 Appeals_
Resolution ALJ-377 established the Citation Appeal and General Order 156 Appeal process (April 28, 2020) based on
* * *
the pilot program established by ALJ-299 (June 26, 2014). Under ALJ-377, appellate records are easily accessible, thus enhancing due process in these expeditious proceedings. Appendix G shows that 37 such appeals were active during 2024 and that the Commission has issued 15 resolutions and 2 decisions addressing the appeals. Twenty appeals are active.
* * *
## _Appendix HRequests for Hearing on Administrative Enforcement Orders Active During Calendar_
Year 2024
* * *
Resolution M-4846 established the process to Request a Hearing on an Administrative Enforcement Order. Under Resolution M-4846, requests for hearing follow the procedural rules set forth in Resolution ALJ-377 that provide easily accessible appellate records thereby enhancing due process and transparency of the Commission Enforcement Policy. One proceeding was active during 2024.
* * *
## _Appendix I – 60-90 Day Period for Adoption of Decision_
The Legislature has also established guidelines for the length of time between the issuance of a proposed decision and
* * *
the adoption of a final decision by the Commission, applicable to all ratesetting proceedings and to quasi-legislative proceedings requiring a hearing. The guidelines are either 60 or 90 days depending on certain circumstances.
* * *
During 2024, the Commission considered 123 proposed decisions subject to these guidelines. Thirteen proposed decisions are pending resolution. The Commission adopted 108 decisions subject to these guidelines. 100 decisions were adopted within the guidelines. Eight proposed decisions were resolved outside the guidelines. One proposed decision was withdrawn at the April 18, 2024 Commission Meeting. One proposed decision was superseded by a May 10, 2024 proposed decision.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 6
* * *
555639775
* * *
## _Appendix J – Issuance of Presiding Officer Decisions and Proposed Decisions_
The Legislature has also established guidelines for the length of time between the submission of a matter for decision
* * *
and the issuance of the proposed decision. During 2024, the Commission issued 13 presiding officer decisions and 124 proposed decisions in such proceedings. Out of these 137 decisions, 87 were issued within the 60-day and 90-day timelines. Two proceedings required oral arguments after the proposed decisions were issued; consequently the submission time was inapplicable.
* * *
## _Appendix K – Issuance of Extension Orders and Scoping Memos_
The Legislature has also established a process for extending the statutory deadlines through issuance of an extension
* * *
order. During 2024, the Commission issued 116 extension orders in 101 separate proceedings (more than one extension order was issued in some proceedings), including proceedings which remained open at the end of 2024. The assigned Commissioners issued 130 scoping memos (including amended scoping memos) in 124 proceedings.
* * *
## _Appendix L – Commissioner Attendance_
## _Appendix L reports Commissioners’ attendance at hearings during the period. The table shows that Commissioners_
attended 65 days of hearings.
* * *
## _Appendix M – Information on Disposition of Applications for Rehearing_
## _Appendix M reports information on the disposition of applications for rehearing in 2024._
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 7
* * *
555639775 Conclusion
* * *
In summary, this report, submitted in compliance with Public Utilities Code Section 910.1, provides the public and the Legislature information on Commission action in formal proceedings. Specifically, 532 proceedings were active at the Commission during the 2024 reporting period. During 2024, 229 of these proceedings were resolved. 98.2% of the proceedings subject to statutory deadlines were resolved consistent with statutory requirements, taking into account scoping memos, which in some instances set deadlines longer than basic statutory timeframes, and orders extending the statutory timeframes adopted by the Commission, as permitted by statute. The Commission is committed to achieving compliance with the statutory guidelines.
* * *
Public Utilities Commission Report Pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 910.1 Page 8
